## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain (mechanical loading) and temperature (thermal effects on material properties like elastic modulus, yield strength, and flow stress).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elasticity with T-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (Hooke's law with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Simple Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (basic linear elastic behavior)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined response)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (modulus with exponential T-dependence)
- Voce hardening with T: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal factor)
- Polynomial in T: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic T-dependence of modulus)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)**(-1)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Hyperbolic sine creep: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)**(-1))) (Garofalo/sinh law for high-T deformation)
- Rational thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 * T + c3)**(-1) (inverse temperature dependence)
- Combined polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T * epsilon (quadratic strain with cross term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) representing decrease of yield/flow stress with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → Terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating stress approaching a saturation value at large strains
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c / T) or exp(-c / T) factors representing thermally activated dislocation mechanisms
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing work hardening in metals (Hollomon exponent typically 0.1-0.5)
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) reflecting separable mechanical and thermal contributions
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appearing as (T - c0) or (c0 * T) representing normalized temperature relative to melting point
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and nonlinear term (epsilon**n) capturing initial elasticity followed by hardening
- Negative temperature coefficient → Coefficients of T terms are typically negative, reflecting material softening at higher temperatures

## Analysis

Let me analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression carefully:

**GT:** `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-36.95/(8.314*T)) - 0.215*(T - 331.68) + 3.554*(T - 331.68)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Expanding:
- `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T)` — a term with `epsilon^0.614 * exp(-const/T)`
- `-0.215*T + 0.215*331.68` — linear in T
- `+3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 3.554*331.68*log(epsilon+1)` — T*log(epsilon+1) and log(epsilon+1) terms

So the GT contains these key structural elements:
1. **`epsilon^0.614 * exp(-const/T)`** — a fractional power of epsilon times an Arrhenius-type exponential in T
2. **`T*log(epsilon+1)`** — T multiplied by log(epsilon+1)
3. **`T`** — linear in T (constant coefficient)
4. **`log(epsilon+1)`** — logarithmic term
5. **A constant term**

Now let me check each candidate. The critical features to match are:
- The **`T*log(epsilon+1)`** term: Most candidates have `T*c*epsilon` (T times epsilon) but NOT `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Only candidate 24 and 32 have `T*c*log(c*epsilon+1)`.
- The **`epsilon^0.614 * exp(-const/T)`** term: This is a very specific nonlinear coupling. None of the candidates contain `exp(-const/T)` or `exp(1/T)` type terms.

**Candidate 24:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*log(c2*epsilon+1) + c3*sin(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6*sin(c7*sqrt(epsilon)+c8)`
- Has `T*log(epsilon+1)` ✓
- Has `T*epsilon` (can absorb linear T term? No, we need plain T, not T*epsilon)
- Missing `epsilon^0.614*exp(-const/T)` ✗
- Uses sin functions instead — sin can't reproduce `epsilon^0.614*exp(-const/T)` for all epsilon and T

**Candidate 32:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*log(c2*epsilon+1) + c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + c5*log(c2*epsilon+1) + c6 + c7*sin(c8*sqrt(epsilon)+c9)`
- Has `T*log(epsilon+1)` ✓
- Has `log(epsilon+1)` ✓
- Has constant ✓
- But has `T*epsilon` instead of plain `T` — could we set c0=0? Then we lose the T*epsilon term but we still need `-0.215*T`
- Missing the `-0.215*T` term (no standalone T term unless absorbed somehow)
- Missing `epsilon^0.614*exp(-const/T)` — has `exp(c4*epsilon)` which is fundamentally different (depends on epsilon only, not T)

The fundamental problem is that **no candidate** contains:
1. A term like `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` which couples epsilon and T in the specific Arrhenius way the GT requires
2. Most candidates lack `T*log(epsilon+1)` 
3. Even candidates with `T*log(epsilon+1)` lack the Arrhenius term

The GT has a complex two-variable coupling through `epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T)` that cannot be reproduced by any combination of the terms available in the candidates (which use products like `T*epsilon`, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, sin, polynomial, and simple exponentials in epsilon).

No candidate can match the GT for all values of both epsilon and T.

Conclusion: No match

- `sin(...)` terms
- `log(c*epsilon + 1)` terms
- Polynomial terms in epsilon
- Some have `T*c*epsilon^2`, `T*c*log(...)`, `exp(c*epsilon)`

**Critical missing elements in candidates:**
1. **`exp(-c/T)` or `exp(c/T)`**: The GT has `exp(-36.95/(8.314*T))`. None of the candidates have any exponential function of `1/T`. The exponentials in candidates are `exp(c*epsilon)`, which is fundamentally different.
2. **`epsilon^c` with fractional power**: The GT has `epsilon^0.614`. Only Candidate 21 has `epsilon^c8` and Candidate 34 has `epsilon^c8`, but they still lack the `exp(-c/T)` coupling.
3. **`T*log(epsilon+1)`**: Some candidates have `T*c*log(c*epsilon+1)` (Candidates 24, 32, 44). But they still lack `epsilon^0.614*exp(-c/T)`.

The term `epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T)` is essential and cannot be approximated by any combination of `T*epsilon`, `sin(...)`, `log(...)`, polynomial terms, or `exp(c*epsilon)`. These are linearly independent basis functions.

Even candidates with `T*c*log(epsilon+1)` (like 24, 32) capture one aspect but cannot reproduce the `epsilon^0.614*exp(-c/T)` term with any constant assignment.

No candidate contains the essential `exp(-c/T)` dependence that appears in the GT. Since `exp(-c/T)` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in T, 1/T^5, linear T, sin, log, exp(c*epsilon)), none of the candidates can match the GT.
